UPPER REGION AGRICULTURAL DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
Planning, Evaluation and Monitoring (PEMD)
Evaluation
1.        The development proposals contained in this report are expected to
have a far-reaching effect on the Upper Region farmers and on the economy of
the nation as a whole; there is, therefore, a high demand for an effective
evaluation system to be implemented both as an aid to Project management and
as a means of permitting effective supervision and impartial assessment of
Project performance. The results of a steady, ongoing evaluation would also
meet the requirements of planners in the preparation of new development in-
vestments.
2.        Project evaluation would center around the following objectives:
(a) establishment of a baseline data survey that would enable
further measurements to be made to determine changing patterns
of farming, farmer response to Project action, and incremental
farmer incomes due to Project investments;
(b) evaluation of Project services including extension, nutrition,
farm input distribution, broadcasting and education programs;
this evaluation would include proposals for improvements that
would be made to broaden the impact of Project actions;
(c) a broader evaluation to determine the secondary impact of
Project actions on regional trade, markets, etc. Such infor-
mation could lead to computation of factors reflecting multi-
plier effects of the Project.
3.        To collect these data, a substantial data collection system would
be established comprising mobile teams of enumerators stationed at each
district. These enumerators would be supplemented by the development of an
overall Project cost/data retrieval system to be established at the outset
of the Project and incorporated in all Project recording processes. Standard
methodology would be used in sample analysis, and particular attention would
be paid to modified systems being developed in Bank-financed projects in
Nigeria. All this information would be held in a central Project data bank
and would be retrievable for use in quarterly and annual reporting, work
planning, etc. The Project would, where possible, use extension staff and
local leaders in a constant evaluation of socio-economic objectives.



ANNEX 10
Page 2
4.        For more detailed and independent analysis of collected data, and
for certain specialized undertakings, PEMD would contract with the Institute
of Statistical, Social and Economic Research (ISSER), Lagos.
Monitoring
5.        PEMD would undertake a constant monitoring of market and price
trends for regional crops. The prime objective would be to speedily and
accurately collect market information, to provide price information and market
opportunities to Project farmers, as well as to assist farmers in marketing
methods. To undertake this work, a special facility--market information
services--would be set up under PEMD. For details see Annex 1, para 10.
Planning
6.        The information collected by the evaluation work will not only
benefit the Project and the nation in evaluating the effectiveness of Project
action, but it will also provide accurate information that can be used in
future planning. In particular, the Project would provide for the planning of
those areas freed of onchocerciasis in the Upper and Northern Regions, details
of which can be found in Appendix I of this Annex.
March 31, 1976



ANNEX 10
Appendix 1
Page 1
GHANA
UPPER REGION AGRICULTURAL DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
Economic Development of Areas Freed from Onchocerciasis in
the Upper and Northern Regions
1.        An FAO/IBRD report 1/ published in October 1975 outlined proposals
for planning economic development in five West African countries in the Volta
River Basin area afflicted by onchocerciasis, or riverblindness. The proposed
planning would cover those areas to be cleared of the black fly Similium
damnosum under the current eradication scheme. In Ghana the onchocerciasis
areas fall within the Upper and Northern Regions, which together total
98,000 km .
2.        The basic planning methodology evolved at the interagency meeting
in December 1974 for the oncho areas has been accepted by the five partici-
pating countries, and is designed to lead to the preparation of:
(a) an inventory of natural resources (the Data Bank);
(b) a broad Ten-Year Development Plan identifying priority zones
of the oncho areas (the Ten-Year Development Plan); and
(c) a number of specific investment projects within the frame of
the Development Plan (project preparation).
3.        The execution of the above would have the long-range objectives of:
(a) improving living standards for those already living in or near
oncho areas, and providing opportunities for settlement in the
relatively fertile oncho areas;
(b) achieving such settlement without the uncontrolled exploitation
and lack of conservation that have characterized most human
settlement in West Africa; and
(c) increasing the national outputs of food, livestock, and
industrial and export crops.
1/   Report No. WS/H3291, Economic Development of Areas Freed from
Onchocerciasis in Dahomey, Ghana, Mali, Togo and Upper Volta.



ANNEX 10
Appendix 1
Page 2
4.        The FAO/IBRD proposals recommended that the planning should be
undertaken mainly by foreign consulting firms; however, the Ghanaians have
specifically requested a high degree of Ghanaian involvement in the planning
process. In order to accommodate the Government's views and to ensure ade-
quate financing, and because the Upper Region is more affected by onchocer-
ciasis than are other areas of Ghana, and implementation of the Upper Region
Agricultural Development Project coincides with the onchocerciasis planning
period, it is proposed that the Project's Planning, Evaluation and Monitoring
Department (PEMD) be responsible for undertaking direct data collection
and planning for the Upper and Northern Regions. Thus a special Onchocer-
ciasis Survey Unit would be established within PEMD. This would have the
advantage of making use of Project specialist staff and equipment; of making
possible the preparation of development plans in association with an ongoing
and related development Project; and of fully integrating Ghanaian staff into
the planning process. The Unit would operate for at least three years and,
apart from its own staff, would draw on other Project staff, non-Project
Government staff (particularly Ministry of Agriculture planners), and con-
sultants including university staff and specialized personnel recruited from
within and outside Ghana. The Ministry of Economic Planning would have
ultimate responsibility for clearing the Ten-Year Development Plan and sub-
sequent related feasibility studies; in this respect it would be important
that the Oncho Unit's planners ensured that development proposals formed
part of the overall national development plan.
Details of Execution
5.        Completion of Data Bank.  Much information already exists for both
Regions; numerous surveys have been undertaken. The Oncho Survey Unit would
complete the Data Bank for each Region, including determination of present
land use; land suitability classification; climate, surface and ground water
resources and potentials; socio-economic data on population, land tenure,
and social organization; and key data relating to agriculture, livestock,
forest and fishery activities.
6.        For the Region concerned, a land suitability survey with mapping
was completed by FAO in 1967. However, an updating of existing land use is
required; this would be undertaken in each area. In the Upper Region, the
analysis would form a part of the integrated evaluation of the Project, making
use of LANDSAT imagery and 1:40,000 infrared color photography. In the North-
ern Region, LANDSAT imagery only would be used. In both cases the Project
would let a contract to a foreign company with the necessary skills and
electronic scanning analysis devices.
7.        A socio-economic study would be undertaken to determine the current
extent of social and economic activity in both Regions. The appraisal report
for the Upper Region would form the basis for that Region's study, to be
updated and expanded where necessary. The study for the Northern Region
would require full documentation. The Oncho Survey Unit would acquire con-
sultant staff on a direct-hire basis for this purpose.



ANNEX 10
Appendix 1
Page 3
8.        It is expected that the Data Bank would be completed within one
year of inception and that the bulk of the data would be available within
six months. Separate summaries would be produced for each Region, cross-
referenced to filed and recorded information.
Ten-Year Development Plan
9.        After six months of data collection, a Development Plan would be
prepared using information from the Data Bank. The head of the Planning,
Evaluation and Monitoring Department, through the Oncho Survey Unit, would
be responsible for its preparation, and would, if necessary, be able to call
on consultants on a short term basis. The Plan would:
(a)  identify, in detail, zones and projects suitable for develop-
ment over the next decade; and
(b) rank the zones and projects identified on the basis of
priorities; that is, according to cost/benefit, impact,
replicability, spread effects, savings/earnings of foreign
exchange, and social benefits.
10.       It should be noted that the Upper Region Agricultural Development
Project already forms a basis for a Ten-Year Development Plan for that
Region; any new plans would investigate and include specific projects in
areas not covered by the Project, such as settlement schemes related to
specific valleys. For the Northern Region, the Development Plan would need
to cover both oncho areas and areas not infested. In formulating the Plan,
due consideration should be given to:
-    maximizing employment opportunities;
-    ensuring equitable income distribution;
-    reducing disparities of income/employment opportunities
between different regions and groups;
-    providing sound land tenure arrangements;
-    simple and effective soil and water conservation methods;
-    increasing production and quality of food, industrial and
export commodities;
-    reducing imports;
-    improving health, nutrition, and educational standards;
-    alternative project proposals maximizing returns with the
lowest cost incentives;



ANNEX 10
Appendix 1
Page 4
-    using the maximum amount of local expertise; and
-    minimizing potential conflicts between groups/individuals as
a result of settlement/repopulation.
11.       The Plan, supported by charts, graphs, maps and such other docu-
mentary references, would take into account any existing Government plans for
the oncho areas and, where necessary, incorporate (with or without modifica-
tion) the existing plans into the Plan, or recommend their deletion or re-
classification in the list of development priorities.
12.       To assist the Oncho Survey Unit in preparing the Plan, the Ministries
of Agriculture and Economic Planning would provide staff, particularly exper-
ienced economists, from their own planning units in Accra. This would provide
a two-way service in that central Government could be directly involved in the
Plan preparation and would provide expertise already existing in the country,
and the Oncho Survey Unit would provide a much needed field for training in
practical planning. The Plan would be completed by the end of the second
year, and would then be fully discussed and cleared with the relevant Minis-
tries in Accra, particularly Agriculture and Economic Planning.
Preparation of Investment Studies
13.       In general, preparation of investment projects would not begin in
detail until after a thorough review of the Development Plan had been under-
taken by Government and after the views and assistance of potential external
financing agencies had been sought. It is expected, however, that a start
would be made to rough out some investment projects concurrent to work on the
Ten-Year Development Plan. Some of these would be prepared by the Oncho
Survey Unit, whereas others could be undertaken by other agencies, such as
German Technical Assistance in the Northern Region, CIDA, USAID, etc. In
any event, if other agencies are involved in planning, they would coordinate
their activities with the Unit.
14.       Further technical details can be found in the FAO/IBRD report
WS/H3291, dated October 1975.
15.       Costs.  Funds would be provided under the Project to meet the
incremental costs required to undertake the studies. 0737,000 has been
specifically allocated against the Oncho Survey Unit's budget. These funds
do not include aerial photography, LANDSAT or analysis for the Upper Region;
neither do they include any costs of Government staff who may be seconded
for a short period to the Unit from other agencies. A breakdown of costs
is at Annex 11.

the Onchocerciasis Survey Unit are as follows:
